> [Quoting nanningbob](/thread/post/4886661#post4886661 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> For example if we could do the RMB because it stays very stable and not move would probably be a big money maker if it was trade able.
> 
> Ignored

%   
  
I am now in the process of setting up an account to trade the RMB or USD/CNY as it is called. The key factor I am looking at is the swap. Since the currency pair is stable the 6.5 overnight rate of the CNY becomes very attractive. Also, long term, it is hard to imagine this pair breaking 7.0. So downside risk, while it exists, is very small. In a 10 year window, breaking 5.0 is much more likely.  
  
At 6:1 leverage, the overnight rate works out to about 20% return per year. The 5 percent appreciation this year would have packed another 30% return.  
  
The possibility that it will rise to 7.0 is small, but it does exist. However, the Chinese government is a big fan of stability. It does not like to surprise its people with the "unexpected". So you will have a lot of advanced warning.  
  
Not relevant, but hopefully you will find it interesting.

Hi Nub. Can't say I am happy to see you, but it is NB's thread so whatever he is comfortable with, I will respect.  
  
I have two points:  
  
1\. Leverage exists in all markets, but the extreme leverage of 500:1 or 100:1 or even 50:1 does not exist in most markets.  
  
2\. That some retail trades never see the light of day does not mean that no retail trade sees the light of day. At least three types of retail trades make it to the interbank market: 1. the large ones, 2. the successful ones and 3. when the trades at a broke become unbalanced, brokers hedge their risk.

  * Oct 12, 2011 11:36am  Oct 12, 2011 11:36am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar121345_4.gif) nubcake](nubcake)

> Disliked

> Hi Nub. Can't say I am happy to see you, but it is NB's thread so whatever he is comfortable with, I will respect.  
>    
>  I have two points:  
>    
>  1\. Leverage exists in all markets, but the extreme leverage of 500:1 or 100:1 or even 50:1 does not exist in most markets.  
>    
>  2\. That some retail trades never see the light of day does not mean that no retail trade sees the light of day. At least three types of retail trades make it to the interbank market: 1. the large ones, 2. the successful ones and 3. when the trades at a broke become unbalanced, brokers...
> 
> Ignored

  
ok i'll bite on this one because it's not completely bonkers...  
  
1\. perhaps. however, just because forex is leveraged so high doesn't mean a thing except that the price movements are so small that it requires the position to be leveraged for the miniscule movements to equate to anything.  
  
it's like, if eur/usd was actually sitting at $120.39 and the spread was $0.01 and the pip size was $0.01 you probably wouldn't have much leverage used on this pair if any at all by anyone. you can probably open positions with what you make in a few weeks wage and actually have it return (or lose) a real amount of money because of the granularity of pip movements..... but the reality is something different. the reality is that the pip size is actually $0.0001 with a spread around that to 2x that. you aren't going to get anywhere waiting for price to tick up 1c without opening a huge position, and if you don't have the money to actually do this then you rely on leverage and margin instead.  
  
what it's NOT like is if eur/usd was trading at $1.0001 and the spread was $0.01. then you'd be a crazy to bother leveraging a position based on this.  
  
all that matters is tick size and spread size. all movement thereafter and leveraging of said movement is purely a function of the tick size and spread.  
  
as for your point number 2.... so if one does not leverage their trades they are not going to be making much money unless they are starting with a mountain of capital in the first place. so, you think that no trader gets into trading with a grub stake, uses leverage, builds a nice bankroll and starts trading size that puts them into ECN and actually affecting liquidity? i'm sure there are some people who jump straight in with their daddy's oil fortunes propping them up, but i do not believe that the majority of retail traders who are actually a part of the market liquidity all come from rich backgrounds and instead actually had to build their capital from a grub stake.... and so i'd love to know how you do that without using leverage!  
  
the conclusion to this is that from what you are suggesting you either start with enough capital to not be leveraged yet still be in the real market trading real volume with size, or you start with a small stake and not be leveraged and so will never see the real market and will always be small fry due to never accumulating a bankroll that supports large trading volume that would put you out of bucket shops and onto an ecn. you aren't ever going to get kicked out of a bucket shop trading nano lots, despite however big your account is. 

Congratulations ScalaFX for coming out of the closet!

  * [#259](/thread/post/5036129#post5036129 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 13, 2011 11:30am  Oct 13, 2011 11:30am 

  * [ Frodog](frodog)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [104 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=106966)

Hi Bob, can you tell me why this would not work?  
  
Some traders in the US are annoyed about not being able to hedge. I have an idea that effectively does the exact same thing.  
  
Censura hedges at 100 and recovers later and this is considered a good strategy, effectively limiting DD.   
  
Why not just set a 100 pip SL using a trade once 1hctr ea. When the stop gets hit, just wait and re-enter when the daily chart indicates a ranging market. This is what would be done with a hedge anyway (close the winner and re-enter in the original direction) The trick when using a SL would be to re-enter at a larger lot size just as you effectively would be with a hedge trade.   
  
Hedge example:  
Buy 1 lot. Trade goes -100 so 1 lot sell hedge trade is taken. Close winner and re-enter 1 lot in original direction using OI recovery ea. TP 50 pips to BE. Exit trade.  
  
SL example:  
Buy 1 lot. Trade goes -100 and hits SL. Set OI recovery ea at 2 lots with 50 pip TP. Once TP is hit, exit trade.  
  
To me the outcome and risk of these examples are the same. The SL example would also save you swaps waiting for recovery ea to enter. Can you tell me how my reasoning is flawed? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#260](/thread/post/5036150#post5036150 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 13, 2011 11:46am  Oct 13, 2011 11:46am

> [Quoting Frodog](/thread/post/5036129#post5036129 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Bob, can you tell me why this would not work?  
>    
>  Some traders in the US are annoyed about not being able to hedge. I have an idea that effectively does the exact same thing.  
>    
>  Censura hedges at 100 and recovers later and this is considered a good strategy, effectively limiting DD.   
>    
>  Why not just set a 100 pip SL using a trade once 1hctr ea. When the stop gets hit, just wait and re-enter when the daily chart indicates a ranging market. This is what would be done with a hedge anyway (close the winner and re-enter in the original direction) The trick...
> 
> Ignored

In other words take 100 pip SL and then pretend you are recovering the SL. Interesting concept. I dont know the percentage of trades that may go 100+ pips down but then retrace and later make a profit. In other words I never have to make it up with a different trade. A different trade would mean I have a whole different set of parameters to meet to make a trade. I do know one thing the win percentage would go down and you would face having to have bigger wins to over come the 100 SL. So let us say your average win is 40 pips. You now need 2.5 wins for every loss just to break even. That is what I had to do before I started range trading or CT trading. You can try but I never could make it work. The two formulas that seem to work for traders is: lots of small stops and have some big winners OR lots of winners that overcome the occasional losers. Something in between I have never seen work. The only way to really tell is to test it out for a month and see how you do.

For example there is this guying trying to get me to use his method of trading. The first trade I took I set up a pending sell just below a major support line. Price breaks support and goes down. Price moved to the exact point, took the trade and then shot back up above the line and headed for the SL. In other words I have to deal with the computer programming within MT4 dealers that are designed to take trades close to moves or SL or account margin calls, widening margins as price moves to TP line, etc. again. To me those are the things that make trading so hard, the odds are so stacked against you.

Exact same as using a stop, then price retracing. If you don't have a predetermined amount of negative pips before hedging (fundamentals) well that would be a different strategy.   
  
But I think if your strategy is to hedge at a set amount of pips every time, it may be easier just to use a stop, and enter the next trade as a recovery trade.

  * [#265](/thread/post/5036236#post5036236 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 13, 2011 12:28pm  Oct 13, 2011 12:28pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar183218_3.gif) AaronWard](aaronward)

  * Joined Jun 2011 | Status: Chilling in Florida | [3,232 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=183218)

> [Quoting nanningbob](/thread/post/5036150#post5036150 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> In other words take 100 pip SL and then pretend you are recovering the SL. Interesting concept. I dont know the percentage of trades that may go 100+ pips down but then retrace and later make a profit. In other words I never have to make it up with a different trade. A different trade would mean I have a whole different set of parameters to meet to make a trade. I do know one thing the win percentage would go down and you would face having to have bigger wins to over come the 100 SL. So let us say your average win is 40 pips. You now need 2.5 wins...
> 
> Ignored

NB,  
  
I played around with something that I called "return to sender" a few months back. Key idea is that once price moves 15 pips off of open price, it returns to that open price more likely than not. Basic contrarian trade.   
  
I used 4 opens and 1 close. Japan open, Frankfurt open, London open, US open, London close. My success rate was just about 90% if I used a 105 pip stoploss. If I used no stoploss, then typically only 3-4 trades did not return to the open/close price within the month. This worked well on the euro/usd and the gbp/usd.  
  
I added a pyramid function. At -30 pips I added a position, at -45 another at -60 yet another. Lot size was determined at 10% risk... if I lost all four trades, then it I would lose 10% of my account. With the stoploss I would typically double my account most months. But a couple of the months I would get badly clipped by a volatile market. Determining lot size as a percentage of account meant that you would never get a margin call, but if your trades went against you it might approach zero.  
  
I tried to manage this with hedging, but found that any mechanical rule I followed created as many problems as it solved. If price movement was clean, then I won. But more often than not, price movement would move on both sides of the -105 pip line, sometimes as many as 50 times. Over time, the [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") became a concern, and the losses (say 10 pips or so) an even greater concern.  
  
I though this system was too dangerous to trade live, and couldn't find a practical way to use the hedge.

> Ignored

You are range trading and the range is too tight. Any move outside the range destroys the concept, moves that stay inside work great.   
  
The key to hedging is knowing when to unhedge it. You can not undo a hedge in a trending market. You have to wait for a ranging market to unhedge it. Unless you have a specific unhedging plan, hedging doesnt work or is extremely difficult to do. Until 10.0 and having a definition of a ranging market I didnt have a good plan to unhedge a hedge except to take my profits from other trades to BE. Now I have an area I can undo the hedge. Once you get into a ranging market, close one at the high and the other at the low. That cleans out the hedge go back to trading and you avoided a very bad trade.

  * Oct 13, 2011 12:53pm  Oct 13, 2011 12:53pm

The concept of recovery trading is If a trade is 100 pips down and I put a recovery trade on I only need 50 pips to break even. Even smaller if i go a little bigger lot ( do not double that is dangerous). In a SL you need to regain the full 100 pips in recovery you only need 50 that is the big advantage of recovery versus SL. That is why your win percentage is higher and why it is easier to overcome DD instead of SL。

  * [#271](/thread/post/5036319#post5036319 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 13, 2011 1:11pm  Oct 13, 2011 1:11pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar183218_3.gif) AaronWard](aaronward)

  * Joined Jun 2011 | Status: Chilling in Florida | [3,232 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=183218)

it seems that the key advantage of hedging is psychological, not mathematical. If you like ranging markets, you get caught in a trending market, and you hate taking a loss, then you can hedge until you get back to the trending market.   
  
But some people will end up paying a high psychological price -- more positions to worry about and a continued sense of something not being resolved.   
  
There is an actual monetary cost to hedging, but it is very small. It is the swap. With two positions open, you will always lose a little on the swap. You may have the spread on an additional position to pay for, but that depends on your subsequent strategy.  
  
IMHO the decision to hedge should be based on "what is better for me" instead of "what is better". One key edge in forex is to to align your strategy with your psychological make up, not against. The actual cost of the hedge -- the swap-- is pretty close to irrelevant to most short term or medium term trades. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Oct 13, 2011 1:25pm  Oct 13, 2011 1:25pm 

  * [ Frodog](frodog)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [104 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=106966)

> [Quoting nanningbob](/thread/post/5036286#post5036286 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> The concept of recovery trading is If a trade is 100 pips down and I put a recovery trade on I only need 50 pips to break even. Even smaller if i go a little bigger lot ( do not double that is dangerous). In a SL you need to regain the full 100 pips in recovery you only need 50 that is the big advantage of recovery versus SL. That is why your win percentage is higher and why it is easier to overcome DD instead of SL。
> 
> Ignored

If you use a stop at 100pips and then reenter at the same lot size you will need 100pips to BE.  
  
If you use a stop and then reenter at the same lot size the hedge would of been, you would then only need 50 pips to BE.   
  
When closing a hedge you then reenter in the original direction, thus increasing original lot size.  
  
If a stop was used, and you reentered at the equivalant hedge lot size, you would still BE at 50 pips.

I have a theory of hedging and had a hedging demo trades going before the USA changed. The great part is I could trade with much larger lot sizes and my gains were quite large. When the USA market was done and prices were ranging I took out the profit at its high or low and let the other retrace and with a CT trade. The size of the CT trade was dependent on the move for the day. Dang that worked well. Was kind of fun to do. Used the 4H high low to get out and trading time was just a few minutes a day.

  * [#277](/thread/post/5036378#post5036378 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 13, 2011 1:47pm  Oct 13, 2011 1:47pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

Yes, that is the understanding. 50 pips is easier to recovery than 100. The key is to reenter with some kind of skill. The bigger the DD the more CT trades you need to over come but you never have to recover the same distance back to 0. One of the things I am learning is I tried to recover using one or two trades. Now I am using smaller profit trades and reducing the DD lot size a piece at a time. The benefit of this is the margin usage goes down even though price may have just stalled somewhere.   
  
If a stop was used you would need to double the lot size to BE at 50. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

  * Joined Jun 2007 | Status: Teach men to fish | [7,384 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41648)

With a short explanation here with the aud/usd. Let us say you have a hedge going. At area 1 is when ranging period would begin. You would try to pick a low and high to release the 2 hedges. See 1A to 1B in second chart. To eliminate 100 pip hedge in this 250 pip retracement. This one would be difficult to read and pick up but it shows it possible. release one near the bottom S line and release the other near the top R line. If that didnt work then on to area 2. You have a 5 day ranging period here.

Area 2 on this chart is a much bigger area and gives a 350 space to unhedge over 3 days. What is nice about this one is a high and low is established before ranging begins.

  * Joined Jun 2007 | Status: Teach men to fish | [7,384 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41648)

Area 3 is a straight reversal into the new trend so that would be hard to unload here. Not a good range but then life is like that sometimes. But that is the theory behind it. Wait for a time when you can unload off of a high low point on a lower chart. I am sure top to bottom BB bands would work also. It is just a matter of catch some kind of low and high to do it in and the range period in 10.0 would be your best explanation.

Yes I think there is a feel for the market. The best thing to use would be the 4H high low because that would give you the range to expect. So if the pips between the high and low are 75 you can capture 40-50 of the pips. You can do the math from there. The problem is since I cant hedge I dont have the practical experience to go with theory. I do have the practical CT trade but not the other. The problem with hedging is not the strategy it is the getting out. The other strategy would be to hold the hedge until you have enough winners to delete it, then you can wipe it out.

I only use EAs to enter. Some of my 4H ones have a tp built in but they are seldom hit (a problem I will deal with this weekend.) I usually take profit at a S/R spot and then set the EA up for another entrance. I take profit sometime into a session. 2-3 hours into JPY, 3-4 hours into the Euro and 3-4 hours into the USA session. Sometimes there is something before the jpy open. I like to grab profit before it retraces back into oblivion. Sometimes I miss the big move but most of the time I get the profit and later get a reentry for another.

I do something similar. I manually set my entries, but have a tendency to close them before I hit the TP. I actually see this as a bad thing. 80% of the time the price actually ends up at the TP, and so I am short changing myself. this really adds up. Over time it works out to about 40% less profit. I see this as a personal failing. My entries are clever, but my exits are driven by fear. But then again, I have not done a proper analysis losses I avoided by exiting too early.

  * [#291](/thread/post/5040145#post5040145 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 14, 2011 1:49pm  Oct 14, 2011 1:49pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

  * Joined Jun 2007 | Status: Teach men to fish | [7,384 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41648)

My view of hedging is an emergency stop the action. It freezes time and allows me to think of what I want to do next. It is a breather. I can walk away for 2 weeks if I want to and come back later. Under pressure you can make some really bad decisions. With it you can think it through exactly what you want to do. It gives you time to make a solid plan and also research how you got into the mess in the first place. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Oct 15, 2011 11:20pm  Oct 15, 2011 11:20pm 

  * [ yonnie](yonnie)

  * Joined May 2008 | Status: Trader | [1,158 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69076)

NB,  
  
dont know how you calculate the volatility of a pair, but I look at the difference between high and low of the last year as a percentage of the low.  
  
the best pairs are usd/cad 7.4%, gbp/cad 7.5%, usd/hkd 7.9%, eur/cad 8.2%, gbp/usd 9.3%, eur/gbp 9.6%, aud/cad 9.6%, usd/sgd 10.5%, eur/aud 10.9%, aud/nzd 12%, usd/jpy 12.6%.  
  
however to look back for a year might be too long, because markets do change quickly.   
  
another way could be to look at the daily ATR for the last month as a percentage of price and trade the ones with the lowest for the next month.  
suppose a daily ATR of 120 pips in a pair priced at 0.60 is twice as volatile as 120 pips in a pair priced at 1.20..........  
  
how do you do the process NB?  
  
now CHF is aligned to the EUR would that make a difference in the volatility?

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

> [Quoting yonnie](/thread/post/5043360#post5043360 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> NB,  
>    
>  dont know how you calculate the volatility of a pair, but I look at the difference between high and low of the last year as a percentage of the low.  
>    
>  the best pairs are usd/cad 7.4%, gbp/cad 7.5%, usd/hkd 7.9%, eur/cad 8.2%, gbp/usd 9.3%, eur/gbp 9.6%, aud/cad 9.6%, usd/sgd 10.5%, eur/aud 10.9%, aud/nzd 12%, usd/jpy 12.6%.  
>    
>  however to look back for a year might be too long, because markets do change quickly.   
>    
>  another way could be to look at the daily ATR for the last month as a percentage of price and trade the ones with the lowest...
> 
> Ignored

  
I have my results in the 10.0 folder. It is in an excel sheet if you want to look.

  * [#305](/thread/post/5088839#post5088839 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 1, 2011 7:19am  Nov 1, 2011 7:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

  * Joined Jun 2007 | Status: Teach men to fish | [7,384 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41648)

OK I had my first losing month this year but I got my recovery. The concept of using all my profit at the 15% mark to reduce DD worked very well. Much better than waiting until 20% DD and taking losses. You will see by my chart where I took losses at 20% and then I used profits to reduce DD above 15%. I kept doing this until my DD was under 10% and then I started pocketing profits again. So if you look at the chart you see where my equity line stayed level and then when my target of 10% was reached I continued taking profits and letting break evens with each pair take care of itself. During this process I kept using the same lot size instead of increasing it. So if I had 3 lot on a pair I would reduce it to 2 but my countertrade was 3. This way I kept my DD down by not not increasing my lot size but still getting the larger lot to reduce my smaller lot. This worked very well once I got the hang of it. See pic below. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

  * [#311](/thread/post/5112106#post5112106 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 8, 2011 6:51pm  Nov 8, 2011 6:51pm 

  * [ The flame](the*flame)

  * | Joined Dec 2009  | Status: Pips brewer | [210 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=128268)

hi bob, i found myself pretty confident with a little mod of this ea: istead of buying and selling directly when ma low or high exit the bb, i set that as a condition and then it waits for a turn.  
example: sell when ma high exceeds bb high in the current or the previous candle AND price is below or equal the previous low.  
in this way u totally avoid runners and enter the trade only when price moves in the right direction!  
i backtested it and found that even if u enter a couple aff pips lower in selling or higher in buying, u rarely incurr in runners or at least u enter in a better position because price has to movo higher (before buying) or lower (before selling)...  
just my 2 pips (i dealed with somme runners using this ea...)  
  
ps. consider the "anti intervention mod" triggering ctr trades only when atr1 M1<atr60 M1 as explained by scooby!

I mean I would rather spend my time figuring out how to make more money or the system better, than wasting time responding or just reading posts from those who just want to stir the pot.  
  
Anyway, getting on to the positive, I have had very positive results with CTR 1H, 10.0 trend trading on the daily and the recovery system. You can trade Forex like equities, similar to an investment manager. That is the way I trade equities, so these systems work well with my style of trading. I have begun to work on 10.1 and a methodology for the stops to try and diversify that part of my trading. I will expand on it in the trend thread. Although, I have asked myself a time or two, why change what is working so well and divert my time doing it?   
  
Bob, thanks for the concepts of your systems and sharing with the community.  
  
Best of trading to all.  
  
George

#  [](/thread/308310-nb-100-range-trading-system)Nb 10.0 range trading system

  * [#321](/thread/post/5148532#post5148532 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 19, 2011 12:16pm  Nov 19, 2011 12:16pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar185500_2.gif) George Adams](george*adams)

  * | Joined Jul 2011  | Status: Investor & Trader | [138 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=185500)

I thought I would post this here, since it pertains to range trading, although this response was in the trending thread.  
  
I went back to my CTR 1H trade results and did a review of the data. Actually, should have done this along time ago, but wanted to see if my perception of the AUD/NZD was correct. Actually, it was not that bad, but the negative part of the perception is one trade I needed to go to L3 to recover, so that probably stuck in my head vs. the shear % of trades which you need to recover from. Anyway, from the time CTR came out to end of summer, here are some results from 7 pairs listed by:  
  
Trades with no recovery needed / Trades needing recovery / % of trades with no recovery  
  
GBP/CAD - 16/3 - 84.2%   
AUD/NZD - 19/3 - 86.4%  
NZD/JPY - 17/2 - 89.5%  
CAD/JPY - 24/2 - 92.3%  
NZD/CAD - 14/1 - 92.8%  
USD/JPY - 12/0 - 100%  
EUR/GBP - 48/0 - 100%  
  
The GBP/CAD & AUD/NZD were the worst performers of my group, as well as once they got away, they ran into L2 and L3 for recovery. The others in the group just moved to another level and just ranged again, so recovering from those were much easier. No doubt the EUR/GBP seems to be the ultimate range trading pair. After seeing this information and for some fun, I think I will demo the CTR 1H in the "trending" market times and see if the results are similar and increase the lot size a bit on the EUR/GBP.   
  
Hope the above is helpful. Next summer when I am definitely back into range trading, I am going to steer away from the AUD/NZD and GBP/CAD.  
  
Best of trading to all.  
  
George

I used median of the BB to set a stop to BE. If it stalled or I saw a reversal pattern on a smaller timeframe, I would take profit. It was mostly manual last time, with some TP hitting the other band. This demo run I have added two items to help with less manual involvement on the exit: MPTM set to 40/10 and Squalou's daily SR indicator. If the other band is below a daily SR, I will set the TP just above/below the SR line vs. waiting for the other band. The other area I am going to evaluate is the entry with the SR indicator. Ideally, I would like to get entries just prior to a daily SR line.   
  
Once I get the demo account linked up with myfxbook, I will send a link for people to follow.  
  
Best of trading to you...  
  
George

  * Nov 25, 2011 5:49am  Nov 25, 2011 5:49am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar41648_3.gif) nanningbob](nanningbob)

  * Joined Jun 2007 | Status: Teach men to fish | [7,384 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=41648)

Egads, why anyone would do a buy on a euro now I dont know. Neither trade makes much sense to me at this point, anyway it has been done, now what? Just some pointers.  
  
Lot size is way out of proportion to account size. I would be trading .10 lots with 5000 dollars. The fastest way to get killed in this business is greed.   
  
You need to get rid of that buy at some point so look for the best bounce you can get and close it out. The sell probably will work if you pick a good spot to get out of the buy. Hopefully price will go back up to that Daily line and you can get out of the buy and then go back down and save your sell. Dang you just cant trade this way, you have no wiggle room to get out of a jam.

This is just my opinion, most likely this is what i would do.

Well by what I see, after getting over the lot sizes and similar issues, you need to learn how to use the system. I do know people using it on the 5M chart but thats because they like it. If you are just learning stick to the 4H and daily charts. That is what most people will be referring to here and what I think are just easier to use.   
  
Also when did you open the trades? The picture you posted is a little small when I try to open it. If they where opened this week you have all the news out of Europe coming out and on top of that U.S. holidays so markets will be out of whack.   
  
You have to look at more than just the system, you may see the S1 and D1 lines on the chart but if you would have looked at the big picture of the whole week with news and holidays you would've known the Euro was a bit hectic.

> Thats hanging around a nice psychological s/r level for me so it might hit it but don't know if it'll break it. I see the euro going down to 1.30 in the near future so I am not sure what to tell you.

The thing is lot sizing properly. Right now it is easy to make money off of the Euro because we all know it has to go down no matter what temporary happy news hits for the short term. Until the Euro gets a more permanent answer to their problem I cant see it going up, only re-tracements.   
  
However, his lot size is so big that he must have a perfect move up to release the buy and the perfect move down to release the sell otherwise his account is cooked. I would at least play for the perfect move that price may rebound but that would be a tough play. Then his last choice would be to close the buy and play the sell but if the rebound is strong he would get into trouble on that trade also.  
  
one penny per 500 dollars and learn the business after that you can go to bigger things.

I would like to add to Gustav answer. I look at percentage of account increase. If you can consistently hit 5-10% a month you are in the professional trader field. Too many people get the idea that this is an easy million. It is not. I know there are people who do better but they are a rare lot. So trade small and learn. It goes like this, if you trade one penny on a 1000 dollar account you would have to lose 100,000 pips to lose all your money. If you do that you know that Forex trading is not for you. If you trade 10 cents you would have to lose 10,000 pips to lose all your money. If you trade 1.00 lots you would have to lose 1000 pips to lose all your money. 1000 pips loss is easy to do. 10,000 pips I think is much harder to do. 100,000 pips, never heard of anyone doing that. My question is this. How much tuition are you willing to pay to learn this business. If you are a rookie, losing a 1000 pips in one month, heck in one week is very doable. Do you want to pay 10.00 dollars, 100.00 dollars or 1,000.00 dollars in tuition???? The choice is yours. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * Nov 28, 2011 11:57pm  Nov 28, 2011 11:57pm 

  * [ Kelisa](kelisa)

  * | Joined Dec 2010  | Status: Swings and Breakouts | [413 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=164333)

Shady,  
  
After reading the past few pages of your post, I see that you are too eager and impatient to trade. Typical of many traders, including myself. I was once an impatient trader who thinks I know how to scalp but end up wiping out 2 live accounts eventhough my max lot size was 2 lots only.   
  
In summary, I guess its better you FULLY understand how NB10.1 works: Daily SR, H4 SR and over market sentiments. Look at Daily for DT or UT but market sentiments prevails. Then, go down to H4 or H1 to make a more precise entry. An entry means on a retracement and not chase the PA.  
  
Practice a demo account too until you can constantly make +pips. Then only you can pull the trigger on the live account.  
  
Believe me, it pays to be patient. imo

Good advice, also trade lot sizes that you can go to bed and sleep and not worry about it wiping your account on a big move. I shoot for 10% a month, I have found out if I try for more I end up in doo doo land. This may surprise you but I only trade one penny per 500 dollars in my account. That is very safe and would take 50,000 pips in losses to wipe out, yet I can make 10% almost every month. Learn this one lesson and you can become a successful trader. Once you get experience you can go for the occasional home run but it seems the smaller I trade the more money I make. LOL if that makes any sense to you. I can outlast any market move and countertrade it back to 0 loss. That keeps my equity curve constantly going up. Took me years to learn that lesson. Doesnt mean it is for everyone but I am totally relaxed if something goes wrong. For example, my computer went out yesterday at home and didnt know how my trades were going until today when I came to work. Had a bunch of nice profits, however, if everything had gone against me my account was in no danger. That is how I live in this Forex jungle. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [#355](/thread/post/5356253#post5356253 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 6, 2012 1:24am  Feb 6, 2012 1:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar185500_2.gif) George Adams](george*adams)

  * | Joined Jul 2011  | Status: Investor & Trader | [138 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=185500)

From my post back in November about the effectiveness of the EUR/GBP, I have completed 2 months of testing with the pair. Two areas I incorporated on somewhat of a manual basis was trying to enter closer to S/R levels and using ATR (average true range). So, if I was on the computer and the pair was breaking the band, I would turn off the EA and let it run to the S/R level or the majority of its ATR, then would turn on the EA for entry. I could not execute this every time, but a fair number of trades I was able to manipulate for better entry.  
  
From the results, 35 trades were taken and none needed recovery. This was one area I was curious about - can the pair range in the trending time as it did in the summer time? There were 6 losses (5 of them were buys) which is 83% winning %. You will notice in month 1, both buys and sells were taken. For month 2, I only took sell orders. The second month was much more effective due to the fundamental state of the EUR. So, from the testing, I feel positive about moving on to try and optimize the EA a bit more and run this all year long.  
  
For the next testing period, I have adjusted the EA to try and simulate the entries I was doing manually, which looked more optimized than the current 1H CTR. Here are the parameters for the entry:   
  
\- 3MA is above/below BB   
\- Price has moved back below/above BB  
\- Daily ATR is at 75% or more of ATR 14.   
  
We might find the ATR criteria will restrict our entries too much, but it does provide good protection for those times when the bands are tight, then price moves, such as Monday morning, London Time. We might need to adjust down a bit on the 75% number.   
  
For the exit, I am going to start with a 30 Pip TP. If we are optimizing the entry based on the full range, hopefully we can achieve above 60%+ of the range for TP. The ATR has been running about 55 Pips. Again, I will be adjusting the TP manually when needed around S/R lines.  
  
Here is the link to the myFXBook account for details. I have been messing with a few other things on the account, but you can see EURGBP trade results.  
  
[https://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/1...1h-demo/195168](https://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/100-ctr-1h-demo/195168)  
  
George

I am testing a slightly different version with an ATR function included as I discussed above. I tried to simulate those manually on some trades during the testing. We will see if it will be more effective on entry or not.

10.1 is a manual system that uses pending orders. 10.0 uses EAs to place orders when you see certain conditions exist. After the EA places the order you manage the trade. Now unless you want to sit at your screen all day looking for the perfect entrance you can use EAs. That is what I use them for. Now if you dont want to use EAs you can use pending orders which are nothing more than an EA used by the dealer. Yes it is an EA. A computer program places your order when price crosses some line on your screen. My EAs do the same thing, place an order when price crosses a line on your screen. Now if you are so anti EA that you wont use pending orders then your alternative is to sit in front of a screen all day waiting to place an order by pushing a button. I have better things to do. Sorry if this came across a little harsh but I get tired of the crowd that criticizes EAs but then uses pending orders which is the same thing just different location of the computer.

I believe EAs work if you manage them. In other words play babysitter. I use them when I see a set up I like and then turn the EA on to take the trade. Better than sitting at the screen all day. My point on pending orders is a computer program takes the trade when price hits the line or point you want. EAs do the the same thing. From studying charts and EAs I discovered that most ideas for EAs are profitable is you babysit them. I have an EA I am testing now that backtest a 80%+ win ratio but you need to take out the occasional losers manually. If you do this then the EA will work.

If you are configuring EA, I think the one which should advance to the forward test is the one which give less drawdown not the one with biggest profit. I think avoiding risk came first, I choose configuration that give less drawdown.   
  
I attach the complete result. I found an interesting fact that currency pair moves differently in a downtrend and in an uptrend. As you can see, the period that I use start at higher price point relative to the point when it ends. But the result is that buy strategy overall gave less drawdown(risk) and bigger profit. The buy EA strive in a downtrend and in an uptrend, but the sell EA strive only in a downtrend while it survive in an uptrend(the profit graph flat). The first graph I attach is the buy EA balance the second one is the sell EA, the period I used is in the third graph.  
  
Add: I had a weird result using the same setting for EURUSD and GBPUSD pairs, the drawdown is somehow too low and the profit is too big. The period used is longer from 2006 which is three times the period of test in USDCAD. The chart attached in the bottom.  
  
Add2: I think it happened maybe because the lower spread on those pairs.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar215704_3.gif) Passerby](passerby)

  * | Joined Jan 2012  | Status: Droid master | [894 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=215704)

> [Quoting nanningbob](/thread/post/5389447#post5389447 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> **I believe EAs work if you manage them. In other words play babysitter.**
> 
> Ignored

What you said is proved in my backtest![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1). Further looking at CTR H1 result and comparing them to daily chart, I understand that what you said in 10.0 booklet help to avoid some of the big looser trades. What I notice is when open price above/under the two MA using CTR H1 could lead to a big loss.   
  
BTW, I do a small modification to your EA. To trigger a trade the difference of the two MA should be at least 9 and the entry is 9 pips earlier. By limiting a trade with 9 pips difference on the two MA you got less trade, and by entering 9 pips between the fast MA makes you trade more. Overall the trade is 20% - 30% less than the original EA but average profit are bigger.  
  
The downside of the backtest is I couldn't change the entry size(lot size) according to balance size. When your account grew you keep gaining/losing same amount of profit/loss. This could be seen in the balance chart, the longer it runs the lesser the slope. The strenght is your system in a backtest is the use of a non repainting indicators, well at least not after the candles close. I use every tick from M1 to simulate a real time trading, it takes longer and the data period is shorter but the result are more valid.  
  
I use 1 lot because it's easier to see how much your profit/loss as 1 pips in 1 lot trade is $10.  
  
PS: Right now I'm playing with your trending EA. I haven't take look deeper how day to day trade in the result I post earlier.

For the next testing period, I have adjusted the EA to try and simulate the entries I was doing manually, which looked more optimized than the current 1H CTR. Here are the parameters for the entry:   
  
\- 3MA is above/below BB   
\- Price has moved back below/above BB  
\- Daily ATR is at 75% or more of ATR 14.   
  
From my last post, I believe I have the EA working now with the above modified criteria from CTR 1H and now ready for a demo testing run. Below is a screenshot of the first trade on the account and I marked the entry location of both. Looks like the above version on this one would have improved by about 13-15 pips. The interesting thing to evaluate over the two month or so is how many trades will it take with the ATR criteria compared to the current CTR 1H. However, from the looks of the chart, it seems to handle a nice run pretty well. Here is the link to the myFXbook account, which I created for this next run if you want to follow along.  
  
[https://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/e...gu-fade/248350](https://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/eg-range--gu-fade/248350)  
  
Best of trading to you all.  
  
George

> [Quoting campco](/thread/post/5406300#post5406300 "View Quoted Post")

>  Ben
> 
> Ignored

Ben,  
  
I am having an issue with the myFXbook systems I have set-up. Some are set private and some public. For some reason it is blocking all. So, what I did for this test run is set up a trade explorer here on FF. If you go to my homepage you will be able to see it there. It is called E/G CTR 1H. I am testing another EA on the G/U and that is different. Only the E/G trades apply to the CTR 1H.  
  
The indicators are all the same as Bob's CTR 1H, except I added the ATR function and moved the trigger point of the trade when the price comes back into the BB vs. when it exits outside the BB. Below is the criteria for a trade.  
  
_Indicators:_  
  
Moving Average, Period = 3, Shift = 0, MA Method = Linear Weighted, Apply to = Low (blue line on chart)  
  
Moving Average, Period = 3, Shift = 0, MA Method = Linear Weighted, Apply to = High (purple line on chart)   
  
Bollinger Bands, Period = 20, Shift = 0, Deviations = 2  
  
PivotsD_v5, I only use this indicator for the info box in the upper left corner which shows daily range (ATR), 14 day ATR, spread, etc. It does alot more with pivot lines, etc. but I set those with the background color because I don't use them.  
  
_Entry Rules_  
  
1\. Price and 3MA must break above BB  
  
Then  
  
2\. When price crosses back into BB AND Daily Range (ATR) > 75% of ATR 14 - Take the trade  
  
_Exit Rules_  
  
Start with 30 pip TP and adjust with S/R. I don't use the other side of the band as an exit.  
  
So, if you look at the enclosed chart in the upper left corner, the ATR 14 is 54.2 Pips. 75% of 54.2 is 40.7 Pips. That means we will not take a trade until the daily range of the pair has reached a range of 40 Pips. The idea here with this criteria is to let the pair get almost to full range, then hopefully come back in the range for a trade. It also protects you against those times where the band is tight and then takes off. Instead of taking the entry at only 20 Pips of range, it waits until 40. The testing will prove if this is really effective and can help improve entries for better pips per trade.  
  
Now, out of all the trading in the summer and this winter, the last trade on EUR/GBP is now requiring recovery. We will see how this goes and I will continue to take shorts trades as they emerge with the EA.  
  
Enclosed is a template which shows all the indicator set-up and the PivotsD.  
  
Hope all that answers your questions. Good trading to you...  
  
George

OK lets say you are at 4 lot, even numbers makes hedging math easier. you are 100 down. If release your hedge and all you want is break even. subtract the profit, lets say 50 pips you would set your trade at 4 lot and would need 25 pips to break even. present trade +25 profit trade +50 losing trade now at -75  
  
Let us say you want to keep your profit and you are down -100 then at 4. you need +50 to break even, lot 6 +33 to break even and lot 8 plus 25 to break even. I think. So that would be the strategy and the math. You can correct my math if I am wrong, I dont have my calculator with me.

Yonnie, it is crucial that you learn how leverage and margin works. How big you can trade with a $10,000 (or any size) account entirely depends on your margin/leverage rate. (But how big you *should* trade is a different matter altogether!) Anyway, a broker with 50:1 leverage will lend you 50x your margin (account balance) which means the maximum trade size you can open is something less than or equal to 50x your account balance. Similarly, if your account is $10,000, then a leverage rate of 50:1 implies that to open a trade of $10,000, which as an aside is unleveraged (and assuming you can in fact do this subject to lot size minimums and so on), would require 1/50th or 2% margin used (think deposit) to open. So you'll open the $10,000 trade, and $200 of your $10,000 will be held back as deposit against your open trade, leaving the remaining $9,800 free for other trades.  
  
Different brokers/account also have different lot sizes: A standard lot in forex is 100,000 units of currency, a mini lot is usually 10,000 and a micro lot is 1,000 units. You should know what your lot size and minimum trade size is, so that you can calculate the actual number of units and consequent value of your trades.   
  
For example, if you trade 1 standard lot, of say usd/jpy, then you'll have bought (or sold) 100,000 units of USD, priced in Yen. This would mean that on a $10k account you'd be leveraged 10:1 on that position. This is already IMHO a dangerous level of leverage for a single position. Another example, if you trade 1 mini lot of GBP/USD, then it means you buy (or sell) 10,000 units of GBP, or about $15800 worth (assuming a GBP/USD exchange rate of 1.58). On a $10,000 account this is therefore about 1.58x leveraged, which is much safer but still slightly leveraged.   
  
Again, do not overleverage, ensure you understand your nominal (effective) leverage of your open positions against your account balance. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

_Buy Setup  
  
When 3MA goes under lower Bollinger band 1.0 deviation, EA will enter a buy.   
  
EA will take profit when 3MA goes above upper Bollinger band 1.0 deviation.   
  
If position goes into a negative 100 pips, manually perform a recovery by going to the 4 hour chart and wait for candle to close above both 3MA and Bollinger upper band 1.0 deviation and enter another buy position to average down. Close both positions when the summation of both position shows a break even. _  
  
Is my understanding correct? Any part wrong?  
  
More Questions :  
  
1)From what I understand, this EA cannot be left totally on its own. When a position goes into red, we need to babysit and manually try to get ourselves out of the bad position using recovery. Most of the time, u post forward testing performance. But Post 363, Passerby performed a back test. Did he use a SL instead of recovery? I couldn’t visualize how to back test the baby sitting steps. If we want to fully automate this EA, and we are compelled to install a SL, what would be an appropriate SL?  
2)Is the BB standard deviation supposed to be 1 or 2. You indicated 1 instead of 2 in your booklet, but I saw some people using 2. If I am not wrong, George Adams is using 2.  
  
Hope u can clear my doubts. Thanks!!

_Buy Setup

It is hard to backtest this because I will use recovery. you can backtest using a SL but to me SL are flexible depending on fundamentals. If I know a strong fundamental is working I dont trade this method. For example I stopped last fall with the Euro news. I still think you can trade this with certain non volatile pairs like the aud/nzd gbp/cad etc. I am not at this time using the method though because the Euro zones difficulties. Greece, Portugal, Spain, Italy, Ireland, and then French banks could be in deep doo doo at any time. I do not wish this but I recognize that instability can hit the market at any time.

I am not at home and will need to get back to you on this one.   
  
Hope u can clear my doubts. Thanks!!

  * [#402](/thread/post/5641165#post5641165 "Post Permalink")

  * May 6, 2012 11:29pm  May 6, 2012 11:29pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar185500_2.gif) George Adams](george*adams)

  * | Joined Jul 2011  | Status: Investor & Trader | [138 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=185500)

Friends, first let me apologize for what I would consider to be a poor test from an execution perspective. I made a number of errors, which really skewed my feeling of the effectiveness. Some of those were letting a couple trades hit the BB on the other side and exiting (most on the losses, which I did not want) and opening multiple positions, when I did not want to. The other issue I ran into was time to allocate to managing the test. As traders, I am sure you all have a few systems you are evaluating or improving upon, with each taking time. As you succeed in some of those projects, those of course warrant more time. As you will see from the results, we would have been profitable, however, in the spirit of finding an improvement over the last test, I don't believe that has been accomplished.   
  
Here are my thoughts on the ATR test:  
  
1\. The entry point was spot on with the EA, which would take entry when the price broke thru the BB, the 3MA was above/below the BB, price came back and broke back through the BB and 75% or more of the ATR was reached. As you can see, a number of criteria is required for entry and that limited the number of trades it would take. The original CTR H1 would almost take trades daily, but this was maybe 1-2/week. I do know, there were a number of trades missed due to the ATR function, which would have done well.  
  
2\. Out of the trades taken, there were 2-3 which required a second entry. So, in this test many more recovery trades required on average. This leads me to the effectiveness of the ATR criteria. Logically, it makes sense to take a ranging trade when it is at it's daily range. However, in this case when the range is being met, perhaps that is when support/resistance is being broken and the pair begins ranging again above/below your entry.   
  
One thought is perhaps the opposite would work better where we want to avoid those times of reaching ATR due to breaking of SR? Probably in those cases there has been a significant news event driving the higher ATR and do we really want to be ranging that movement. Second thought is I like the entry point better (minus the ATR requirement) of this test vs. the original CTR H1. The CTR H1 takes entry when the price and 3MA have broken the BB. This last test I coded the entry when price comes back below/above the BB.   
  
If I were going to test again, that might be the approach I would take and see if I can achieve better results. As Hans, pointed out, perhaps demo accounts be set up for all 3 options (original CTR H1, with ATR greater than 75%, and ATR less than 75%) to view results for more conclusions.   
  
I hope this is helpful to those of you range trading.   
  
Good trading to you all.  
  
George
